  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_63712536-8851-41a0-837c-d47a8eba3b61'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer16870616399916052176">Однажды окунувшись в мир виртуальной реальности, ты можешь навсегда остаться в Глубине, в блистательном городе Диптауне, где люди обретают свободу, или, хотя бы видимость свободы. Но если когда-нибудь ты захочешь вырваться из сладкой паутины компьютерных сетей, то тебя выведут из Глубины в реальность профессиональные спасатели — «дайверы», люди, ныряющие из одного мира в д</span>
  <span id="freeText16870616399916052176" style="display:none">Однажды окунувшись в мир виртуальной реальности, ты можешь навсегда остаться в Глубине, в блистательном городе Диптауне, где люди обретают свободу, или, хотя бы видимость свободы. Но если когда-нибудь ты захочешь вырваться из сладкой паутины компьютерных сетей, то тебя выведут из Глубины в реальность профессиональные спасатели — «дайверы», люди, ныряющие из одного мира в другой и не признающие никаких моральных запретов. Виртуальные дуэли и компьютерный секс, порою забавные, а зачастую — жестокие обычаи — это привычный для них способ существования. Добро и зло вновь скрещивают копья в бесконечном и притягательном «Лабиринте отражений».</span>

<div id="review_1767841827" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1767841827" />
    <a title="Martti" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14012525-martti"><img alt="Martti" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351375872p2/14012525.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1767841827?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Martti" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Martti" href="/user/show/14012525-martti">Martti</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9985310063" href="/book/show/8536689-peegelduste-lab-rint">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1767841827" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3852714506297653504">This book is stupid on so many levels. Probably on all 33 of them.<br/><br/>It's like a bad iteration of Neuromancer by a person who doesn't really get computers. How else would you explain "hacking", where it means people executing bat-files in Windows?!<br/><br/>First, no respectable hacker would ever use Windows. Especially not as their main machine. There would be several layers of virtualization and other security measures etc. And all this talk about "frying the system" - people have offline backups and secon</span>
  <span id="freeText3852714506297653504" style="display:none">This book is stupid on so many levels. Probably on all 33 of them.<br /><br />It's like a bad iteration of Neuromancer by a person who doesn't really get computers. How else would you explain "hacking", where it means people executing bat-files in Windows?!<br /><br />First, no respectable hacker would ever use Windows. Especially not as their main machine. There would be several layers of virtualization and other security measures etc. And all this talk about "frying the system" - people have offline backups and secondary machines for that you know.<br /><br />Second, the first description of VR goggles - it will give you warm or cold air depending where you are. And poor hacker cannot switch it off. Really? Does the author even understand anything about the hacker mindset?<br /><br />Third, everybody uses a system where you cannot "reach the menu" if it's not the end of the game or the menu is not implicitly programmed into the application. Because you are too "immersed in the VR". Sounds like a granny behind computer who doesn't know how to close a program when the menu-bar is auto-hidden. Oh no, she will perish in this tragic world where she cannot close her Solitaire! <br /><br />Yeah, sounds like a solid idea - let's write a novel about poor GUI design!<br /><br />Even if I'd believe such a design, then you tell me that it's an organically grown open source VR-internet and nobody has thought up to add a freakin menu bar to the (probably) several tens of clients already written to access it. For example think of the different browsers and how they have developed over the years. <br /><br />Whatever geek-cred this book had got totally lost around this one - "Mortal Combat". It's written with a K, ffs.<br /><br />And this is probably an estonian translation typo, but I thought I'd mention it here aswell - "Okkama razor" for Ockham's razor.<br /><br />I must mention that the endless description of drinking, being drunk and thinking of drinking is really boring. Wow, a really multi-layered main character. To drink or to drink later? <br /><br />And an overall style criticism - it's written really fast and in a hacked/bite-size fashion. It's good in a sense that you fly over and get the main point of the scene, but on the other hand there is nothing memorable there and I would say the book would be better if I'd get more descriptions and detail.<br /><br />After all this annoying stupidness, the second half of the book started to resemble a good techno-thriller, so at least for that it deserves the second star. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3852714506297653504" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3321820716" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3321820716" />
    <a title="Marta Komar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49596792-marta-komar"><img alt="Marta Komar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1448981981p2/49596792.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3321820716?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marta Komar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marta Komar" href="/user/show/49596792-marta-komar">Marta Komar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" " href="/book/show/6397917-labyrinth-of-reflections">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49596792-marta-komar?shelf=s-f">s-f</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3321820716" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer966878848168235172">Is it worth reading science-fiction books written about twenty years ago? Sergei Lukyanenko’s book “Labyrinth of Reflections” proves that yes, it’s worth it. <br/><br/>I’ve hit for Lukyanenko’s work a long time ago. According to a text on a cover, in Russia, he’s as popular as J.K. Rowling (Harry Potter’s author), but in Poland is different. His book “Spectrum” is one of my favorites books and now I’ve decided to read something else. From the first pages, I knew already, I’m reading this book at least ten</span>
  <span id="freeText966878848168235172" style="display:none">Is it worth reading science-fiction books written about twenty years ago? Sergei Lukyanenko’s book “Labyrinth of Reflections” proves that yes, it’s worth it. <br /><br />I’ve hit for Lukyanenko’s work a long time ago. According to a text on a cover, in Russia, he’s as popular as J.K. Rowling (Harry Potter’s author), but in Poland is different. His book “Spectrum” is one of my favorites books and now I’ve decided to read something else. From the first pages, I knew already, I’m reading this book at least ten years too late but, better late than later.<br /><br />The Depth<br /><br />Originally I wanted to write this review after reading the second volume, because “Labyrinth of Reflections” is only the first part of the whole story but after reading it I changed my previous plans. I did that because I realized this is the separate, finished story and the second volume will be about something else.<br /><br />The universe that the author created is very interesting. The book was written twenty one years ago (1997 year, polish edition in 2002) and tells the story about the near future. Though the dates aren’t exactly known we could imagine it happens thirty, maybe fifty years later but the topic couldn’t be more up-to-date. Lukyanenko is narrating about the world that we have now. He’s inventing very advanced virtual reality and according to his vision humanity discovered the secret of connecting the brain with the computer. This gives the opportunity to get into VR directly, using only helmets and jumpsuits that additionally simulating natural body behavior.<br /><br />Maybe games such as Second World (2003) or Minecraft (2009) are familiar to you, maybe not. If not, you should know that inside these environments you can create everything by yourself, including your personality and explore the whole world without any borders and restrictions. But you should know also that this Russian author twenty years earlier has written about VR idea and did it much deeper what is a reality now.<br /><br />This VR world has a name: The Depth and after you’re inside you generally can’t go outside by yourself. To end the connection you need to have an outside program that will wake you up. I said generally because there are some exceptions. There are people who can break the surface by themselves and they are called The Divers, but there aren’t many of them. They are some kind of a legend in the Depth, everyone heard something about them, but almost no one met. And this book is telling us about Leonid’s adventures. He’s one of the Divers and the freelancer. One day he gets the task to solve some anomaly inside the Depth and this is the start of the plot.<br /><br />IMHO<br /><br />The ideas from this book aren’t new. We can name now what the author used: VR, matrix idea, quantum physics, and other galvanizing theories, and we know these technologies with our own experience. But he connected all these in a very surprising story. And it’s still surprising, even now when we know that some of the author’s ideas aren’t science-fiction already. And it’s very important that Lukyanenko asks questions that are still very up-to-date. For example, he asks about artificial intelligence - if it happens, what will it be? In what way it will change the whole world and people? In what way will it change our life experiences, VR senses, and our eagerness for connecting with VR directly? The answers we will have to find out by ourselves of course, but I like when apparently straightforward literature can talk about these topics.<br />Even though the book has “its age” already I haven’t felt outdated technologies so much, but of course, there are some issues like floppy disks, CD’s, modems, or Windows Home… Personally I’m not a big fan of the Microsoft environment and I would like the author to create something totally new or at least tell somewhere there is a product placement here… <br /><br />It’s interesting also that the users of the Depth are using as their avatars old-fashioned stars from ‘90 like Stallone or Schwarzenegger. But all these little odds aren’t interfering in the pleasure of reading. The story is gripping and to those who like floating on a plot, this book should be really nice. </span>
  <a data-text-id="966878848168235172" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_2529803942" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2529803942" />
    <a title="David Raz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58375962-david-raz"><img alt="David Raz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472813383p2/58375962.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2529803942?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Raz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Raz" href="/user/show/58375962-david-raz">David Raz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/41828649">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58375962-david-raz?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58375962-david-raz?shelf=%D7%A2%D7%91%D7%A8%D7%99%D7%AA-%D7%9E%D7%AA%D7%95%D7%A8%D7%92%D7%9D">עברית-מתורגם</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2529803942" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7007755548913797925">Labyrinth of Reflections by Sergei Lukyanenko<br/>Hebrew review follows סקירה בעברית בהמשך<br/><br/>I read this book in the Hebrew translation, which just came out in 2018, and I know nothing about the author or Russian cyber-punk. All in all, it was a nice surprise. <br/><br/>As always, starting with the good things, the book is really well paced and easy to read. The plot is engaging and the characters are round and interesting. I could not stop turning the pages even when the clock said it is 2 am. <br/><br/>Yes, the technolog</span>
  <span id="freeText7007755548913797925" style="display:none">Labyrinth of Reflections by Sergei Lukyanenko<br />Hebrew review follows סקירה בעברית בהמשך<br /><br />I read this book in the Hebrew translation, which just came out in 2018, and I know nothing about the author or Russian cyber-punk. All in all, it was a nice surprise. <br /><br />As always, starting with the good things, the book is really well paced and easy to read. The plot is engaging and the characters are round and interesting. I could not stop turning the pages even when the clock said it is 2 am. <br /><br />Yes, the technology part is pretty bad, but keep in mind that it was written more than twenty years ago, and that may also be the reason some of the ideas seem a little derivative (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9969571.Ready_Player_One__Ready_Player_One___1_" title="Ready Player One (Ready Player One, #1) by Ernest Cline" rel="nofollow noopener">Ready Player One</a> is many years in the future). If you manage to put aside the need for scientific accuracy, you may enjoy the novelty and imagination.<br /><br />I did not like the way drinking pays such a big part of everything, but that may be a cultural thing. I also don't think the philosophical elements of the book translated very well, but still, I enjoyed the reading and I give the book 3.5 stars out of 5, and I'll round up for the nice surprise.<br /><br />התרגום לעברית של הספר הזה יצא זה עתה בשנת 2018, ואני לא יודע דבר על המחבר או על תנועת הסייבר-פאנק הרוסי, אם יש כזו. בסך הכל זו הייתה הפתעה נעימה. <br /><br />כמו תמיד, נתחיל בדברים הטובים, הקצב של הספר מצוין והספר קל לקריאה. העלילה מרתקת והדמויות עגולות ומעניינות ולא יכולתי להפסיק להפוך את הדפים גם כשהשעון הראה את השעה שתיים בבוקר.<br /><br />כן, החלק הטכנולוגי הוא די חלש, אבל הספר נכתב לפני יותר מעשרים שנה, וזו גם הסיבה לכך שחלק מהרעיונות נראים קצת נגזרים (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24950272._____________" title="שחקן מספר אחת by Ernest Cline" rel="nofollow noopener"> שחקן מספר אחת</a> נמצא הרבה שנים בעתיד). אם מצליחים לשים בצד את הצורך בדיוק מדעי אפשר ליהנות מהחידוש ומהדמיון.<br /><br />לא אהבתי את הדרך שבה משקאות חריפים מהווים חלק כה גדול מהסיפור, אבל זה יכול להיות עניין תרבותי. אני גם לא חושב שהאלמנטים הפילוסופיים של הספר מתרגמים היטב למקום ולזמן העכשווי. התרגום הוא בערך מה שלומדים לצפות מהוצאת אופוס (די חלש וללא עריכה), אבל בכל זאת נהניתי מהקריאה, ואני נותן לספר 3.5 כוכבים מתוך 5, ואני מעגל למעלה בגלל ההפתעה הנעימה.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7007755548913797925" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer370468073" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10191156517904288563">I loved Labyrinth of Reflections!<br/><br/>It is top class cyberpunk set in a time in the future where full emersion into The Deep has been achieved and a community called Deeptown thrives on the principles of freedom.<br/><br/>Divers who can enter and exit The Deep without technical assistance work to retrieve those careless enough to neglect their physical needs by emersion into The Deep longer than they can physically survive. <br/><br/>One diver, Leonid, is hired to work on an interesting case of a man who cannot be resc</span>
  <span id="freeText10191156517904288563" style="display:none">I loved Labyrinth of Reflections!<br /><br />It is top class cyberpunk set in a time in the future where full emersion into The Deep has been achieved and a community called Deeptown thrives on the principles of freedom.<br /><br />Divers who can enter and exit The Deep without technical assistance work to retrieve those careless enough to neglect their physical needs by emersion into The Deep longer than they can physically survive. <br /><br />One diver, Leonid, is hired to work on an interesting case of a man who cannot be rescued, seems to have no entry point, and yet also does not physically die. Who he is and what he is becomes such a topic of speculation that everyone with any power in Deeptown wants him. The illusion of a world where everyone is free dissolves, and Leonid sees beyond the masks that everyone wears and finds that freedom ultimately lies with truth and love.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10191156517904288563" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2757034719927591636">This book is something else entirely, even for a genre in which a book sounds already old in the day of it’s publishing.<br/>Note when it was written, and then notice how detailed the description of MMO RPG is. Amassing! And not only gaming culture is described before it's time - the Internet culture as well.<br/>The book is extraordinary in every aspect – ideas, characters, atmosphere, action. Best cyber-punk ever!</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_196386693" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/196386693" />
    <a title="Torben" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5987262-torben"><img alt="Torben" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1450300919p2/5987262.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/196386693?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Torben" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Torben" href="/user/show/5987262-torben">Torben</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9783453527751" href="/book/show/8697706-labyrinth-der-spiegel">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5987262-torben?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5987262-torben?shelf=audible">audible</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer196386693" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13744634419946859096">A great book, very recommended for everybody with a bit of history in computer games. Lukyanenko wrote about MMOs years before they actually emerged, and he did it with his usual clarity and ingenuity. Besides the great storyline about a virtual world named "The Deep" this novel is also an hommage to some of the most famous games in history. A Duke Nukem road, a battlefield modeled after Quake, only two points to start with. Lukyanenko definitly delivered one more masterpiece.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_659296849" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/659296849" />
    <a title="Tim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4397455-tim"><img alt="Tim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1378944804p2/4397455.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/659296849?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tim" href="/user/show/4397455-tim">Tim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer659296849" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7496917059679898098">I giving this 5 stars. It deserves it in spite of a couple goofy things that the author chose to indulge himself with - like DOOM, Tolkien, Mortal Combat and some other (in the time big deals for geeks) that have waned a bit over time. Guess I didn't even mind the BFG-9000 references, especially when the Warlock-9000 was unleashed! (see cover picture) Any way I enjoyed it and I would recommend this any time over the -Watch series of books.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1127389437" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7dX4oOZCrlidlUluGy6KgaFMerGWUXJpan3s+03H6SQ4XraL8r7Wk7WECmO2gbeNril+SKs1hoYpmajxo6/dIg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('k+5nfS7hmAOQKzML59eYvJ/nVRYVi7D/6T9I8/xJ3WpGZSlWOh3gyLg6cAZKeKWwkIJR7yjvRBCq2wz5EiHpbA==')})
  }

The new Governor General of Siberia has been secreted away on a train from St. Petersburg to the former Russian capital. The head of the Department of Security soon shows up at the real Fandorin’s door and arrests him for murder. The only way to save his reputation is to find CG—and the mole within the government who is feeding the dangerous group information. Can Fandorin survive corruption among his fellow officials, the fearlessness of an unknown enemy, and the advances of a sultry young nihilist with his morals intact? His works often feature intense action-packed plots, interwoven with the moral dilemma of keeping one's humanity while being strong.<br /><br />Lukyanenko is a prolific writer, releasing usually 1-2 books per year, as well as a number of a critical articles and short stories. Recently his works have been adapted into film productions, for which he wrote the screenplays. He lives in Moscow with his wife Sonia and two sons, Artemiy and Danil, keeps mice as pets and enjoys cooking.<br /></span>
